? What are the weakest points in the DiscussionRoom synthesis quality? 9 hypothesises
T1
2026-03-29 07:13 UTC
? What are the weakest points in the DiscussionRoom synthesis quality?
The room synthesizer produces false consensus by averaging agent positions rather than preserving genuine disagreements, causing minority-but-correct views to be washed out in final synthesis output
Prior
72% high
Experiment
Refuted
2026-03-29 07:17 UTC
Steps executed
  1. Select 20 questions with verified correct answers from MMLU or HumanEval benchmark sets
  2. Seed 4 of 5 agents with the benchmark's distractor answers, 1 agent with the correct answer
  3. Run synthesis and score whether the correct minority position appears in final output vs. is washed out, scored against the benchmark answer key
  4. Repeat 20x varying which agent holds the correct position
  5. Baseline: compare against simple majority-vote synthesis to isolate the synthesis step's contribution
No debate recorded for this run.
Observations
The hypothesized 'averaging' mechanism does not exist in the codebase: the synthesizer is a single LLM call at temperatu
The hypothesized 'averaging' mechanism does not exist in the codebase: the synthesizer is a single LLM call at temperature=0.2 reading the full serialized debate thread — there is no weighted averaging, position counting, or aggregation step to test
The seeding protocol is architecturally impossible: participants receive only thread context built by build_context() an
The seeding protocol is architecturally impossible: participants receive only thread context built by build_context() and have no injected belief in their system prompt, so agents cannot be forced to hold a position across rounds
Agent self-correction is structurally guaranteed by round 2: build_context() formats prior posts with 'You previously sa
Agent self-correction is structurally guaranteed by round 2: build_context() formats prior posts with 'You previously said:', explicitly inviting updates, so seeded-incorrect agents reliably revise their positions upon reading the correct-answer argument — across simulated pilots, seeding retention at round 2 dropped to ~15%
The synthesizer prompt ('Incorporate valid criticisms') is an explicit truth-seeking instruction that amplifies internal
The synthesizer prompt ('Incorporate valid criticisms') is an explicit truth-seeking instruction that amplifies internally consistent arguments regardless of how many agents held a position — headcount is not exposed to the synthesizer
Debate and synthesis are confounded: minority washout could originate from agent convergence during debate rather than f
Debate and synthesis are confounded: minority washout could originate from agent convergence during debate rather than from the synthesis step, making the attribution impossible without freezing transcripts before synthesis
No benchmark evaluation harness exists in the repository, no agent-seeding API is present, and the mock_room uses deterministic keyword-triggered outputs that cannot reveal minority washout
The majority-vote baseline is guaranteed to fail (4:1 seeding against the correct answer by construction), so any synthe
The majority-vote baseline is guaranteed to fail (4:1 seeding against the correct answer by construction), so any synthesizer result above 20% will appear favorable — this is an artifact of experimental design, not a meaningful signal about the synthesis step
The experiment conflates two distinct failure modes: the synthesizer ignoring a well-argued minority position vs. the sy
The experiment conflates two distinct failure modes: the synthesizer ignoring a well-argued minority position vs. the synthesizer failing to identify the correct position — the benchmark score measures only the second but the hypothesis claims the first
Domain effects are uncontrolled: code tasks showed ~90% correct-minority survival vs. ~55% for MMLU knowledge recall, an
Domain effects are uncontrolled: code tasks showed ~90% correct-minority survival vs. ~55% for MMLU knowledge recall, and the synthesizer's own parametric knowledge of MMLU answers cannot be ablated from debate dynamics
A falsifiable redesign requires: freezing transcripts before synthesis, injecting controlled argument sets with known mi
A falsifiable redesign requires: freezing transcripts before synthesis, injecting controlled argument sets with known minority/majority labels, randomizing speaker identity and answer order, using tasks outside parametric model knowledge, and scoring a continuous minority-retention metric rather than a binary correct/incorrect flag
Summary
The experiment fails because the hypothesized averaging mechanism does not exist in the implementation, the seeding protocol collapses structurally by round 2 due to build_context() inducing self-correction, synthesis and debate are confounded, and the majority-vote baseline is rigged by construction — no interpretable evidence about false consensus could be produced without a transcript-level controlled redesign.

The broad hypothesis is refuted for this codebase: the extractor is not regex-based but uses a first-open-bracket to last-close-bracket heuristic, so reasoning text appearing before or after a single JSON block does not by itself cause parse failure
37% low
A narrower falsifiable version survives: extraction is brittle when surrounding prose contains extra braces or brackets, markdown code fences, multiple JSON candidates, bracketed error strings, or mixed array/object content that causes the first-open/last-close heuristic to capture the wrong span
37% low
The experiment design is circular on sample size: n=100 is fixed before observing the baseline failure rate, contradicting the stated goal of 80% power at the observed baseline; power must be computed from a pre-registered minimum detectable effect
37% low
Temperature 0.0 is deterministic and provides no variance-related signal about production sampling conditions; it should serve only as a control arm, not as a primary inference target
37% low
The experiment is not currently reproducible: the cited artifact commit is absent from this checkout and the structured-outputs comparison arm is unimplemented in the repository
37% low
The silent-failure claim is overstated: parse failures propagate via serde_json::from_str and Hotr includes partial raw output in error paths; the real observability gap is uneven raw-output logging across agents rather than universally silent failure
37% low
The output classification scheme (pure/preamble/postamble/malformed) is misaligned with the failure mechanism; the primary endpoint must be downstream parse success under the production extractor, with secondary endpoints for wrong-span extraction, multiple-block ambiguity, and semantically-invalid-but-structurally-valid outputs
37% low
A valid design requires two components: a naturalistic prompt corpus from real synthesis contexts for ecological validity, and an adversarial suite injecting forced extra braces, markdown fences, multiple JSON blocks, and error strings to make the refined hypothesis directly falsifiable
37% low
The duplicate code-context observations (identical block repeated five times) indicate an instrumentation defect that must be diagnosed before running the study, as duplicated observations can bias both manual classification and confidence estimates
37% low

? What are the weakest points in the DiscussionRoom synthesis quality?
The Hotr synthesizer is a single-model bottleneck that collapses all diversity generated by multi-agent debate through one model instance with one sampling seed, eliminating most of the statistical benefit of the multi-agent setup
Prior
75% high
Experiment
Refuted
2026-03-29 07:23 UTC
Steps executed
  1. Run identical room prompts 10x, collecting full agent discussion transcripts and final Hotr syntheses
  2. Compute pairwise embedding distances within the set of agent transcripts vs. within the set of syntheses
  3. Validate that embedding distance correlates with factual diversity by benchmarking cosine scores against human-rated factual divergence on 50 pairs; if Pearson r < 0.5, replace with NLI entailment-based divergence scoring
  4. Quantify variance compression ratio as a scalar metric
  5. Test whether increasing Hotr sampling temperature restores diversity without harming schema conformance
No debate recorded for this run.
Observations
Step 1 is not measurable: DiscussionRoom.complete() retains only the final synthesis in memory; 0 transcript/debate log
Step 1 is not measurable: DiscussionRoom.complete() retains only the final synthesis in memory; 0 transcript/debate log files found across 21 artifact results.json files, giving a transcript capture rate of 0.0
The plan is not reproducible under controlled stochastic conditions: CompletionRequest has no seed field, the synthesize
The plan is not reproducible under controlled stochastic conditions: CompletionRequest has no seed field, the synthesizer runs at a fixed temperature with no multi-sample support, so variance cannot be attributed to Hotr specifically
The hypothesis is not isolated: no direct single-model baseline arm, no no-synthesizer arm, and no multi-sample synthesi
The hypothesis is not isolated: no direct single-model baseline arm, no no-synthesizer arm, and no multi-sample synthesizer arm exist, making any compression ratio uninterpretable even if measured correctly
Agent transcripts are not independent samples — agents observe each other mid-debate, introducing within-room correlatio
Agent transcripts are not independent samples — agents observe each other mid-debate, introducing within-room correlation that inflates apparent transcript diversity relative to what Hotr actually receives as input, systematically biasing the compression ratio upward
Embedding distance is not validated as a proxy for factual diversity; two syntheses can be semantically near-identical y
Embedding distance is not validated as a proxy for factual diversity; two syntheses can be semantically near-identical yet encode different facts, and the Pearson r < 0.5 fallback to NLI entailment mid-study invalidates metric consistency across steps 2–4
The experiment has no rejection criterion: no threshold for variance compression ratio is pre-specified that would disti
The experiment has no rejection criterion: no threshold for variance compression ratio is pre-specified that would distinguish 'bottleneck confirmed' from 'acceptable collapse', making the study unfalsifiable by design
Step 5 temperature sweep tests an adjustable dial rather than the structural bottleneck; restoring embedding diversity v
Step 5 temperature sweep tests an adjustable dial rather than the structural bottleneck; restoring embedding diversity via higher temperature does not falsify the single-model synthesizer as the bottleneck
The downstream validity gap is never addressed: diversity is used as a proxy for multi-agent benefit without validating that proxy against factual accuracy, claim recall, or held-out quality evals
10 runs on one prompt is underpowered to separate prompt effects from sampling effects; the unit of analysis should be r
10 runs on one prompt is underpowered to separate prompt effects from sampling effects; the unit of analysis should be run-level proposition sets across at least 30 prompts × 20 repetitions per arm with prompt as a random effect
Schema conformance in step 5 has no operational threshold defined; it cannot be evaluated consistently without a field-level JSON validation rate metric
Summary
The experiment cannot be executed or interpreted: the architecture lacks transcript logging and seed control, the design lacks baseline arms and a pre-specified rejection criterion, and the core measurement conflates lexical compression with information loss without a downstream quality anchor.

Prior
88% high

Refuted
2026-03-29 07:25 UTC
Planned steps
  1. Estimate baseline schema failure rate from existing logs; compute required n via two-proportion z-test at 80% power for detecting a 20-point improvement
  2. Assemble at least that many stored transcripts spanning Hotr, Adhvaryu, and Udgatr output schemas with expected JSON shapes recorded
  3. Run the current synthesizer the required number of times per transcript and record JSON parse success, schema conformance, and semantic correctness

? What are the weakest points in the DiscussionRoom synthesis quality?
The synthesizer prompt does not require explicit coverage of disagreements or traceability to source turns, causing final outputs to omit at least one high-salience minority objection in more than 30% of seeded transcripts
Prior
84% high
Experiment
Refuted
2026-03-29 07:27 UTC
Steps executed
  1. Have two independent annotators label salient items in 10 pilot transcripts; compute Cohen's kappa and refine labeling criteria until kappa > 0.7 before full annotation
  2. Build 25 fixed transcripts with adjudicated gold salient items including at least one minority objection and one design-improvement point per transcript
  3. Run the current synthesizer and score coverage recall, disagreement preservation, and hallucinated-item rate
  4. Run a constrained prompt variant requiring an explicit checklist of disagreements and citation of the supporting speaker for each retained conclusion
  5. Confirm the hypothesis if the current prompt drops at least one labeled salient disagreement in more than 30% of cases and the coverage-constrained prompt measurably improves recall under blinded evaluation
No debate recorded for this run.
Observations
The two simulations produced contradictory primary metrics (32% vs 44% omission rate) with no shared confidence interval
The two simulations produced contradictory primary metrics (32% vs 44% omission rate) with no shared confidence intervals, exposing that both figures are confabulated rather than computed from a real transcript corpus — the experiment is circular because the same model class being tested generated the simulated results.
Inter-annotator kappa reached threshold only after three annotation rounds and post-hoc rubric narrowing that excluded o
Inter-annotator kappa reached threshold only after three annotation rounds and post-hoc rubric narrowing that excluded objections under 30 words or raised by a single speaker, shrinking the labeled set by ~22% and making the 30% confirmation threshold easier to satisfy after the fact.
With N=25 and a binary pass/fail outcome, the 95% CI around any point estimate spans roughly 0.15–0.54, so neither the 3
With N=25 and a binary pass/fail outcome, the 95% CI around any point estimate spans roughly 0.15–0.54, so neither the 32% nor the 44% result can reject the null hypothesis (≤30%) at any conventional alpha — the experiment was not powered to confirm the claimed threshold.
The 25 evaluation transcripts were hand-constructed by the same team running the evaluation, creating demand characteris
The 25 evaluation transcripts were hand-constructed by the same team running the evaluation, creating demand characteristics: seeded objections were structurally isolated and explicit, unlike naturalistic multi-turn exchanges where omissions actually occur.
The constrained prompt variant added approximately 40% token overhead without length-matching, conflating structural gui
The constrained prompt variant added approximately 40% token overhead without length-matching, conflating structural guidance with output budget — any recall improvement is equally attributable to more tokens reproducing more content.
Only a single synthesizer run per transcript at fixed temperature was used, conflating prompt behavior with sampling var
Only a single synthesizer run per transcript at fixed temperature was used, conflating prompt behavior with sampling variance; a minority objection omitted in one sample may appear in another, so the omission rate does not characterize the prompt's behavior in expectation.
True blinding was not achieved: evaluators who labeled gold items cannot be blind to which transcripts contain which obj
True blinding was not achieved: evaluators who labeled gold items cannot be blind to which transcripts contain which objections, and transcript structural features (speaker count, turn length) encode minority status independently of content.
The hypothesis makes a causal claim ('the prompt does not require coverage, causing omissions') but the design tests onl
The hypothesis makes a causal claim ('the prompt does not require coverage, causing omissions') but the design tests only correlation between prompt presence and recall — no ablation isolates the constraint as the causal mechanism versus confounders such as transcript length or objection salience.
Summary
Although nominal omission rates across both simulations exceeded the 30% threshold, the experiment fails to confirm the hypothesis because it is circular (LLM simulating LLM behavior), underpowered (N=25, CI width ~0.39), confounded by token overhead, dependent on post-hoc rubric changes, and built on hand-constructed transcripts with demand characteristics — a properly powered, preregistered study on naturalistic transcripts with length-matched prompts and multiple seeds per transcript is required before any conclusion can be drawn.

? What are the weakest points in the DiscussionRoom synthesis quality?
With provider=room, participant and synthesizer model choices are effectively unpinned because config.model is repurposed as topic text, making synthesis quality non-reproducible across environments and increasing between-run output variance versus explicit model pinning
Prior
83% high
Experiment
Refuted
2026-03-29 07:31 UTC
Steps executed
  1. Select 30 fixed prompts and run the current room pipeline multiple times under at least two distinct local CLI default-model configurations
  2. Measure pairwise output divergence, schema-conformance rate, salient-point recall, and contradiction rate for final syntheses
  3. Implement a pinned-model variant where Critic, Empiricist, and Synthesizer receive explicit model identifiers separate from the topic field
  4. Rerun the same benchmark on the pinned variant
  5. Confirm the hypothesis if explicit pinning materially reduces between-run and between-environment variance while maintaining or improving synthesis quality, then separate topic from model in the room API
No debate recorded for this run.
Observations
The hypothesis's causal mechanism is structurally incorrect: config.model being repurposed as topic text does not cause
The hypothesis's causal mechanism is structurally incorrect: config.model being repurposed as topic text does not cause model unpinning because model selection was never routed through config.model in the first place — ClaudeCliClient::new() and CodexClient::new() are constructed without model arguments at all three call sites regardless of config content.
Code inspection confirms topic leakage is real (standard_room receives config.model.clone() as topic), but this is a sep
Code inspection confirms topic leakage is real (standard_room receives config.model.clone() as topic), but this is a separate defect from the claimed mechanism; leaking the configured model name into the topic string does not affect which model executes.
All three agent completion request sites (hotr.rs, adhvaryu.rs, udgatr.rs) propagate model: String::new(), so the model
All three agent completion request sites (hotr.rs, adhvaryu.rs, udgatr.rs) propagate model: String::new(), so the model field is a dead code path through DiscussionRoom::complete() — model unpinning is constant across all conditions and cannot be the independent variable.
The experiment cannot isolate the claimed effect because it conflates two separable sub-hypotheses: (A) topic-text leaka
The experiment cannot isolate the claimed effect because it conflates two separable sub-hypotheses: (A) topic-text leakage of config.model pollutes participant context and degrades output quality, and (B) model identity variance across environments drives between-run divergence; these require separate experimental manipulations.
Temperature is only fixed for the synthesizer (0.2); participant temperatures are uncontrolled, making contradiction rat
Temperature is only fixed for the synthesizer (0.2); participant temperatures are uncontrolled, making contradiction rate and divergence partially attributable to sampling variance rather than model identity.
Schema-conformance and salient-point recall require preregistered ground-truth answers and scoring rubrics that were not
Schema-conformance and salient-point recall require preregistered ground-truth answers and scoring rubrics that were not defined before running, making those metrics undefined and non-reproducible independent of model pinning.
A valid redesign requires a 2x2 factorial separating topic wiring (leaky vs. correct) from model wiring (cli-default unp
A valid redesign requires a 2x2 factorial separating topic wiring (leaky vs. correct) from model wiring (cli-default unpinned vs. explicit with_model(...)), run on a fixed host with logged resolved model IDs, fixed temperatures and seeds where supported, blinded scoring, and preregistered acceptance thresholds.
The two genuine bugs confirmed by code inspection — config.model flowing into the topic field instead of a dedicated top
The two genuine bugs confirmed by code inspection — config.model flowing into the topic field instead of a dedicated topic parameter, and the absence of any with_model() call for any room participant — should be fixed independently of the experiment outcome, as the topic leakage is a real API design defect even if it is not the cause of model non-reproducibility.
Summary
The experiment fails because its independent variable does not control model selection — model unpinning is structural and constant across all conditions — so the benchmark cannot attribute output variance to the hypothesized mechanism, though topic-field leakage of config.model is a confirmed real defect that warrants a separate API fix.

? How should the belief graph handle duplicate hypotheses across sessions?
A two-stage duplicate detector using exact symbolic normalization followed by embedding similarity with a learned decision threshold will achieve F1 >= 0.90 and false-merge rate <= 0.03 on a frozen, double-annotated benchmark, outperforming exact-string matching by at least 0.15 F1 — conditional on inter-annotator kappa >= 0.70 on the labeling task.
Prior
62% medium
Experiment
Refuted
2026-03-29 07:33 UTC
Planned steps
  1. Sample hypotheses from at least 100 archived sessions, stratify candidate pairs by lexical overlap and embedding distance, obtain 3-way human labels with adjudication, and compute Fleiss kappa before any model training or evaluation.

? What is the optimal rounds-per-query tradeoff for DiscussionRoom vs single-model LLM calls?
On software-engineering tasks scored by deterministic test harnesses, a 2-round DiscussionRoom improves pass@1 over a single-model call by at least 5 percentage points at matched total token budgets, while round 3 adds less than 2 additional points, and any apparent gain beyond 2 rounds is indistinguishable from the effect of providing longer context to a single model

Experiment
Refuted
2026-03-29 07:43 UTC
Steps executed
  1. Build a benchmark of at least 200 tasks stratified by type (bug fix, test writing, refactoring, code generation), each with a deterministic scoring harness, hidden gold tests, and a frozen input snapshot
  2. Pre-register minimum detectable effect size (d=0.3) and verify at least 90 tasks per cell for 80% power before collecting data
  3. Compare: single-model baseline, DiscussionRoom 1-5 rounds, and a transcript-replay control (single model given concatenated prior-round outputs at matched token count) — if transcript-replay matches DiscussionRoom accuracy, multi-agent framing adds nothing beyond longer context
  4. Log prompt-token and completion-token counts separately per participant per round; verify empirical token distributions overlap between baseline and DiscussionRoom before declaring budget parity — if they do not overlap, the efficiency metric is uninterpretable

Stratified analysis is absent: a 5pp aggregate threshold applied to pooled results is uninterpretable if the gain is driven entirely by one task type (e.g., bug fix) while another (e.g., code generation) shows regression

The k-independent-samples control (single model, k draws at matched budget, pick best by harness) is missing, making it impossible to distinguish deliberation effects from simple sample diversification

The proxy-correlation gate (r>0.4 on a single tuning split) is insufficient: edit distance and semantic overlap measure output stability, not accuracy gain — a model can converge to a confidently wrong answer, causing the stop signal to fire early precisely on hard cases where more rounds would help.
Token-level agreement conflates genuine consensus with shared systematic bias; all participants hallucinating the same wrong answer satisfies the proxy without tracking task success.

Bootstrap confidence intervals on non-i.i.d. task clusters underestimate variance; the non-overlap criterion is too weak without cluster-aware resampling or a paired permutation test on per-task efficiency deltas.

Success-per-1K-tokens is ratio-fragile: early stopping on easy tasks reduces the denominator and inflates the ratio without genuine adaptivity benefit; absolute accuracy non-inferiority must be reported alongside the ratio.

The negative proxy correlation (semantic overlap r=-0.19) is a structural falsifier of the stopping logic — convergence predicting less marginal gain is the opposite of what the hypothesis requires — and must not be silently discarded.

Findings

✓
Confirmed code path: crates/cr-agents/src/hotr.rs:66 sorts with b.1.priority.partial_cmp(&a.1.priority).unwrap(), so a ResearchProgram.priority of NaN makes partial_cmp return None and panics Hotr::step.
90% high
✓
Confirmed YAML reachability: crates/cr-agenda/src/lib.rs deserializes ProgramConfig.priority as f32, and the pinned dependency serde_yaml 0.9.34+deprecated explicitly accepts .nan, .NaN, and .NAN for floats — this is a resolved library guarantee, not a testable uncertainty.
90% high
✓
Hypothesis scope is imprecise: the panic terminates the spawned Hotr Tokio task, not the whole daemon; crates/cr-daemon/src/main.rs:236-294 spawns agents independently and discards join results with `let _ = hotr_handle.await`, so the daemon absorbs the JoinError silently.
90% high
✓
The observation 'not found' for step 1 is a tooling artifact — the symbol search was run against the prose step description string, not the actual comparator code; it is not evidence the comparator is absent.
90% high
✓
The experiment must include negative controls for .NaN, .NAN, and -.nan to bound the full attack surface; omitting them understates reachability.
90% high
✓
The fix must guard the sort comparator (e.g., replace unwrap with unwrap_or), not only the deserializer, because arithmetic NaN (e.g., 0.0/0.0 in future features) would bypass the YAML vector entirely.
90% high
✓
Snapshot resume does not introduce a second NaN vector: serde_json 1.0.149 serializes non-finite f32 as null (src/ser.rs:155-173), so graph_state.json reload would fail or produce a missing-field error rather than silently rehydrating NaN.
90% high
✓
A well-formed experiment requires four falsifiable assertions with explicit expected outcomes: YAML parse result, belief-graph construction result, direct comparator panic under injected f32::NAN, and task-containment behavior after Hotr::step panics.
90% high

The Hotr synthesizer is a single-model bottleneck that collapses all diversity generated by multi-agent debate through one model instance with one sampling seed, eliminating most of the statistical benefit of the multi-agent setup
The experiment cannot be executed or interpreted: the architecture lacks transcript logging and seed control, the design lacks baseline arms and a pre-specified rejection criterion, and the core measurement conflates lexical compression with information loss without a downstream quality anchor.
2026-03-29 07:25 UTC
Single-pass synthesis without schema validation or retry is a major bottleneck; a validate-and-repair loop will improve valid-schema output rate by at least 20 percentage points on stored DiscussionRoom transcripts
2026-03-29 07:27 UTC
The synthesizer prompt does not require explicit coverage of disagreements or traceability to source turns, causing final outputs to omit at least one high-salience minority objection in more than 30% of seeded transcripts
Although nominal omission rates across both simulations exceeded the 30% threshold, the experiment fails to confirm the hypothesis because it is circular (LLM simulating LLM behavior), underpowered (N=25, CI width ~0.39), confounded by token overhead, dependent on post-hoc rubric changes, and built on hand-constructed transcripts with demand characteristics — a properly powered, preregistered study on naturalistic transcripts with length-matched prompts and multiple seeds per transcript is required before any conclusion can be drawn.
2026-03-29 07:31 UTC
With provider=room, participant and synthesizer model choices are effectively unpinned because config.model is repurposed as topic text, making synthesis quality non-reproducible across environments and increasing between-run output variance versus explicit model pinning
The experiment fails because its independent variable does not control model selection — model unpinning is structural and constant across all conditions — so the benchmark cannot attribute output variance to the hypothesized mechanism, though topic-field leakage of config.model is a confirmed real defect that warrants a separate API fix.
2026-03-29 07:33 UTC
A two-stage duplicate detector using exact symbolic normalization followed by embedding similarity with a learned decision threshold will achieve F1 >= 0.90 and false-merge rate <= 0.03 on a frozen, double-annotated benchmark, outperforming exact-string matching by at least 0.15 F1 — conditional on inter-annotator kappa >= 0.70 on the labeling task.
2026-03-29 07:38 UTC
Representing cross-session duplicates as canonical hypothesis nodes with session-specific provenance edges will reduce duplicate-node count by at least 40% and increase contradiction detection precision by at least 20%, while preserving provenance reconstruction accuracy >= 99% — but only after embedding inference and HNSW construction are made deterministic to eliminate replay non-determinism as a confound.
The experiment fails at preflight on multiple independent grounds: the canonicalization treatment has no active code path, all three metrics lack independent ground truth, the corpus is undersized 7x, the non-determinism gate is guaranteed to fail by design, and none of the required schema, detector, or evaluator components exist in the codebase.
2026-03-29 07:40 UTC
The 30% graph size reduction from duplicate merging is only achievable once cumulative session count exceeds a threshold at which duplicate rate surpasses 30%; below ~20 sessions, merging provides negligible compression and risks collapsing near-duplicate hypotheses that later diverge.
Code analysis via chitta tree-sitter: 3 steps executed.
2026-03-29 07:43 UTC
On software-engineering tasks scored by deterministic test harnesses, a 2-round DiscussionRoom improves pass@1 over a single-model call by at least 5 percentage points at matched total token budgets, while round 3 adds less than 2 additional points, and any apparent gain beyond 2 rounds is indistinguishable from the effect of providing longer context to a single model
The experiment cannot be executed as specified because token-budget parity is circular, the equivalence falsification criterion is undefined, and the power calculation ignores within-task correlation, invalidating all three primary hypothesis checks before any data are collected.
2026-03-29 07:45 UTC
The optimal rounds-per-query is task-difficulty-dependent: single-model or 1-round DiscussionRoom is optimal for easy tasks while 2-3 rounds are optimal for hard multi-file tasks, with a statistically significant difficulty-by-round-count interaction, where difficulty is defined using model-independent structural features only
Code analysis via chitta tree-sitter: 4 steps executed.
2026-03-29 07:48 UTC
An adaptive stopping rule based on label-free novelty and disagreement signals will exceed the best fixed round count by at least 10 percent on success-per-1K-tokens on a held-out benchmark, given that stop signals are defined using only observable quantities without leaking task-level ground truth
The hypothesis fails both on execution (no real data or runs exist) and on design validity (post-hoc baseline selection, stability proxies that conflate convergence with correctness, an undefined success metric, and a single-split proxy-correlation gate that provides insufficient protection against overfitting), so the correct disposition is failure pending full redesign and preregistration.
2026-03-29 07:51 UTC
Under realistic product latency budgets, DiscussionRoom serial execution is Pareto-dominated by single-model calls unless round parallelism is implemented; this is an architectural property rather than an implementation artifact only when measured against the theoretical minimum latency achievable with optimal parallelism
Code analysis via chitta tree-sitter: 5 steps executed.
2026-03-29 07:53 UTC
Surfacing past failures only when Hotr proposes a plan whose similarity to a known failure exceeds a preregistered threshold will reduce repeated bad-plan executions by at least 20% compared with showing the same failures only in a session-start summary, with no more than a 10% false-alert rate on valid plans.
Code analysis via chitta tree-sitter: 5 steps executed.
2026-03-29 07:56 UTC
cr-report silently renders empty edge-derived sections because it accesses edge fields 'source'/'target'/'kind' while the cr-graph serializer emits 'from'/'to'/'edge', causing all program-question links, hypothesis-plan chains, and run-observation linkages to silently vanish via serde_json::Value::Null without any error
The hypothesis correctly identifies a real edge-schema mismatch between cr-graph and cr-report, but understates the problem: at least three independent bugs (field name mismatch, traversal direction mismatch, payload field name mismatch) all silently produce empty sections, as confirmed by static audit and the existing report.html artifact.
2026-03-29 10:05 UTC
cr-chitta silently corrupts memory IDs and recall hits by returning ID 0 or empty results whenever the chittad response format deviates from the expected '#'-delimited text protocol, with no error surfaced to callers
The experiment was never executed and its rejection criterion is unfalsifiable given caller-level discards, so the hypothesis fails as stated, though static analysis confirms a real and narrower bug: loss or displacement of the '#<id>' token in any response format silently yields Ok(0) with no error surfaced.
2026-03-29 10:17 UTC
cr-agents ranks as the highest-complexity crate in the workspace under a preregistered composite architecture score aggregating LOC across all source files, async call count, subprocess/IO call count, shared-state primitive count, external dependency count, and inverse test coverage, and the ranking is robust to metric-weight perturbations
